The Third Division of Conditional Syllogisms: Shared Middle Term
Defining the third division of imperfect conditional syllogisms and its two conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the third division of conditional syllogisms and verify whether a given conditional syllogism satisfies the two conditions for productivity.

Core Idea
The third division links the minor's consequent to the major's antecedent via a shared middle term.

In the previous lesson, we learned about imperfect conditional syllogisms. Now we dive into the third division of such syllogisms, where the middle term connects the consequent of the minor premise to the antecedent of the major premise. This division has two specific conditions that determine its productivity. Understanding these conditions allows you to recognize valid inferential patterns in complex conditional reasoning used in Islamic legal and theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the middle term's position
In the third division, the middle term (hadd al-awsat) appears in the consequent of the minor premise (tali al-sughra) and in the antecedent of the major premise (muqaddam al-kubra). Locate these two positions in the syllogism.
This distinguishes it from other divisions where the middle term might be elsewhere.
2
Apply condition one: productive composition
The first condition requires that the two premises (al-musharikan) contain a productive composition (ta'lif muntij). This means the minor must be affirmative and one of the premises must be universal. Check both characteristics.
Affirmative minor and universality of at least one premise are compulsory.
3
Apply condition two: result of composition
The second condition involves the result of composition (natijat al-ta'lif). This result must either be exactly identical to the universal antecedent of the major, or the universal antecedent of the major must produce the negative consequent of the minor. Verify which relation occurs.
This condition ensures the chain is properly closed.
4
Enumerate the six productive moods
Based on the first condition, there are six moods: universal affirmative minor with both universal premises, universal affirmative minor with both particular premises, and particular affirmative minor with both universal premises. List them to confirm familiarity.
These moods are the building blocks for productive syllogisms in this division.
5
Analyse the example given
Examine the author's example: 'If J is D then every A is B' and 'Every time every B is H then W is Z' yields a conclusion involving two conditionals. Trace how the middle term 'B' links the premises and how the result of composition becomes part of the conclusion.
The example illustrates the abstract definition concretely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقسم الثالث من هذا القسم [أي من القسم الثاني وهو غير التام]، هو ما يكون الأوسط مشتركا بين تالي الصغرى ومقدم الكبرى، والشرط فيه على قسمين أيضًا: أحدهما اشتمال المشاركين على تأليف منتج مع إيجاب الصغرى وكلية إحديهما . والثاني إنتاج نتيجة التأليف أو عكسها بكليته مع تالي الصغرى: إما / بعينه بكليته لمقدم الكبرى الكلية، أو إنتاج مقدم الكبرى الكلية لتالي الصغرى السالبة؛ والمنتج بحسب الشرط الأول ستة أضرب، الصغرى الموجبة الكلية مع الكليتين والجزئيتين، والصغرى الموجبة الجزئية مع الكليتين وعدد الضروب المنتجة في كل شكل من الأشكال الأربعة في كل ضرب من هذه الضروب الستة هو عدد الضروب المخصوصة بذلك الشكل لا غير. ونتائجها متصلات جزئية مقدمها موافق للصغرى في الكيف، وتاليها للكبرى. ونتيجة التأليف في هذا القسم تالي لمقدم النتيجة، ومقدم لتاليها كقولنا قد يكون إذا كان «ج د» فكل «أب»، وكلما كان كل «ب ه» فـ «وز» ينتج قد يكون إذا كان (ج) د فكل أهـ فقد يكون إذا كان كل «أه» فـ «وز».
The third division of this division [i.e., of the second division which is the imperfect one], is where the middle term is shared between the consequent of the minor and the antecedent of the major. Its condition is also of two kinds: one, the two participants include a productive composition with the affirmation of the minor and the universality of one of them; and the second, the production of the result of composition or its inverse in its entirety with the consequent of the minor: either exactly in its entirety to the universal antecedent of the major, or the production of the universal antecedent of the major to the negative consequent of the minor. The productive moods according to the first condition are six: the universal affirmative minor with the two universal premises and the two particular premises, and the particular affirmative minor with the two universal premises. The number of productive moods in each of the four figures in each of these six moods is the number of moods specific to that figure, none other. Their conclusions are particular conditionals whose antecedent agrees with the minor in quality, and whose consequent agrees with the major. The result of composition in this division is consequent to the antecedent of the conclusion, and antecedent to its consequent, as in our saying: 'It may be that if J is D then every A is B, and every time every B is H then it is W is Z' yields 'It may be that if J is D then every A is H, so it may be that if every A is H then it is W is Z'.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage introduces the third division of conditional syllogisms within the second main division (the imperfect conditional). The author defines it: the middle term is shared between the consequent of the minor premise and the antecedent of the major premise. Two conditions are given for productivity. The first condition requires that the two premises contain a productive composition with the minor being affirmative and one of them universal. The second condition involves the result of composition or its inverse with the consequent of the minor. Specifically, either the entire result is exactly the universal antecedent of the major, or the universal antecedent of the major produces the negative consequent of the minor. According to the first condition, there are six productive moods: the universal affirmative minor with both universal premises (i.e., with universal major? Actually 'ma'a al-kulliyatayn wa al-juz'iyyatayn' means with the two universal premises and the two particular premises? Confusing. It likely means with two universal premises (both universal) and with two particular premises? But later it says: universal affirmative minor with the two universals and the two particulars, and the particular affirmative minor with the two universals. So six combinations. The author then notes that the number of productive moods in each figure (of the four figures) for each of these six moods is the number specific to that figure. The conclusions are particular conditionals with antecedent matching the minor's quality and consequent matching the major's quality. Finally, the author gives an example: a conditional syllogism where the first premise is a conditional (if J is D then every A is B) and the second premise is a universal conditional (every time every B is H then W is Z), producing a conditional conclusion: 'It may be that if J is D then every A is H, so it may be that if every A is H then W is Z.' This illustrates the structure where the result of composition (the middle term linkage) becomes the antecedent of the conclusion.

Key Terms
القسم الثالث (al-qism al-thalith): The third division of the second part (imperfect conditional) where the middle term is shared between the consequent of the minor and the antecedent of the major. [Note: Specific to this classification; not a standard term in all logic works.]
المشاركان (al-musharikān): The two premises (the participants) that share the middle term. [Note: This term is used here in the context of conditional syllogisms; generally means the two premises.]
نتيجة التأليف (natījat al-ta'līf): The conclusion obtained by composing the two premises, which in this division becomes a term in the final conclusion. [Note: Same as previous lesson but applied differently here.]
الضروب الستة (al-ḍurūb al-sitta): The six productive mood combinations based on the first condition: universal affirmative minor with universals/particulars, and particular affirmative minor with universals. [Note: This specific enumeration is unique to this passage.]

The Second Condition in the Third Division: Eight Universal Moods
Author explains the second condition and its eight moods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the second condition for productivity in the third division of conditional syllogisms and determine the number of moods that yield universal conclusions.

Core Idea
Eight moods emerge when the major is universal and the minor is affirmative, yielding universal conclusions under the second condition.

The author now explains the second condition of the third division. This condition specifies that the result of composing the premises, or its converse, together with the consequent of the minor, must entail the antecedent of the major. From this condition, eight productive moods arise, all with universal conclusions. In this lesson, we will break down the components and see how the moods are counted, despite the passage being incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three key components
Recognize the major premise (universal), the minor premise (affirmative), and the second condition: the result of composition (natijat al-ta'lif) or its converse with the consequent of the minor entails the antecedent of the major.
The condition links the intermediate result to the major's antecedent.
2
Understand why the major must be universal
The author states 'al-kubra kulliya la mahala' (the major is necessarily universal). This ensures that the moods produce universal conclusions, as only universal majors can combine with the condition to guarantee a universal conclusion.
If the major were particular, the conclusion would not be universal.
3
Count the moods from the affirmative minor
The text says 'arba'a min al-sughra al-mujaba' (four result from the affirmative minor). Since the major is universal, the minor can be either universal affirmative or particular affirmative, giving two possibilities for quantity, and two for quality? Actually, only affirmative is mentioned, so these four likely come from the combination of universal and particular affirmative with the universal major, but the text is cut off; the total eight moods presumably include the negative minor as well.
The incomplete passage suggests the other four moods come from the negative minor.
4
Determine why conclusions are universal
The antecedent of the result entails its consequent because the antecedent of the minor entails the consequent of the minor—universally if the minor is universal, particularly if particular. This entailment, combined with the condition, yields a universal conclusion (if the major is universal and the condition holds).
The universal entailment propagates to the final conclusion.

Source Text

وأما المنتج بحسب الشرط الثاني فثمانية أضرب؛ إذ الكبرى كلية لا محالة فيحصل أربعة من الصغرى الموجبة؛ والمنتج مع نتيجة التأليف أو عكسها بكليته لمقدم الكبرى الكلية هو تالي الصغرى بعينه أو بكليته في هذه الضروب الأربعة. ونتائج هذه الضروب كلية لأن مقدم النتيجة مستلزم لتاليها لما أن مقدم مقدّمها الذي هو بعينه مقدم الصغرى مستلزم لتالي الصغرى استلزامًا كليا إن كانت الصغرى كلية ، وجزئيا إن كانت جزئية لإلزامه للمجموع المركَّب من تالي الصغرى. ونتيجة التأليف المنتجين لمقدم الكبرى وهو مع
As for what is productive according to the second condition, there are eight moods; since the major is necessarily universal, four result from the affirmative minor. And what is productive together with the result of the composition or its converse in its entirety for the universal antecedent of the major is exactly the consequent of the minor or in its entirety in these four moods. And the results of these moods are universal because the antecedent of the result entails its consequent, since the antecedent of its antecedent, which is exactly the antecedent of the minor, entails the consequent of the minor — universally if the minor is universal, and particularly if it is particular, due to its entailing the composite totality of the consequent of the minor. And the result of the composition productive for the antecedent of the major is with...
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage begins the explanation of the second condition for the third division of conditional syllogisms. The author states that under this condition, there are eight productive moods. Because the major premise must be universal, four moods arise from the affirmative minor (presumably universal and particular, though not fully stated). The productive result, together with the result of the composition (or its converse in its entirety), yields the antecedent of the major. The consequent of the minor appears exactly or in its entirety in these four moods. The conclusions of these moods are universal because the antecedent of the result entails its consequent. This entailment is universal if the minor is universal, and particular if the minor is particular, due to the antecedent's entailment of the composite set of the consequent of the minor. The text cuts off while discussing the result of the composition that is productive for the antecedent of the major, but the idea is that the intermediate conclusion links to yield a universal conditional conclusion.

Checkpoint
According to the second condition in the third division, how many moods are produced from the affirmative minor?
A) Four
B) Six
C) Eight
D) Two

Key Takeaway
The second condition yields eight moods when the major is universal, with four arising from the affirmative minor, all producing universal conclusions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the following conditional syllogism in Islamic law: 'If the sale is valid, then ownership transfers; if ownership transfers, then the buyer may use the item; therefore, if the sale is valid, the buyer may use the item.' Identify which component corresponds to the result of composition, and verify whether the second condition holds (i.e., does the result of composition or its converse together with the consequent of the minor entail the antecedent of the major?).
?
Construct a compound conditional syllogism from Usul al-Fiqh where the major premise is universal and the minor is affirmative, and then determine how many moods from the affirmative minor would be possible under the second condition.
